<!doctype html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
  <meta charset="utf-8" />
  <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1" />
  <title>Maze of Invisible Walls</title>
  <style>
    :root{
      --bg:`#000`;
      --panel:`#1a1a1a`;
      --game:`#8b0000`; /* dark red central game area */
      --cell:`#242424`;
      --wall:`#3a3a3a`;
      --invis:`#555`;
      --player:`#00c46a`;
      --enemy:`#e60026`;
      --exit:`#1e90ff`;
      --item:`#ffd166`;
      --gap:2px;
    }
    html,body{height:100%}
    body{
      margin:0; background:var(--bg); color:`#fff`;
      font-family:system-ui,-apple-system,Segoi UI,Roboto,Ubuntu,Cantarell,Noto Sans,Arial,sans-serif;
      line-height:1.45;
    }
    .wrap{
      min-height:100%;
      display:flex; align-items:center; justify-content:center;
      padding:16px;
    }
    .shell{
      width:min(1000px,96vw);
      display:grid; gap:16px; grid-template-columns:1fr 300px;
    }
    `@media` (max-width:860px){ .shell{ grid-template-columns:1fr } }

    /* Central game area */
    `#game-area`{
      background:var(--game); color:`#fff`;
      border-radius:12px; padding:16px; position:relative;
      box-shadow:0 12px 36px rgba(0,0,0,.55);
      outline:none;
    }
    `#board`{
      margin:12px auto;
      width:min(92vw,560px); aspect-ratio:1/1;
      display:grid; grid-template-columns:repeat(10,1fr); grid-template-rows:repeat(10,1fr);
      gap:var(--gap);
    }
    .cell{
      background:rgba(255,255,255,.06);
      position:relative; border-radius:4px;
      box-shadow:inset 0 0 0 1px rgba(255,255,255,.05);
      transition:background .15s ease, box-shadow .15s ease;
    }
    .cell.wall{ background:rgba(0,0,0,.55); box-shadow:inset 0 0 0 1px rgba(255,255,255,.08) }
    .cell.invis.revealed{ background:rgba(80,80,80,.7) }
    .reveal-glow{ box-shadow:inset 0 0 10px rgba(255,255,255,.25), 0 0 10px 4px rgba(255,255,255,.2) }

    .entity{ position:absolute; inset:12%; border-radius:50%; display:grid; place-items:center; }
    .player{ background:radial-gradient(circle at 30% 30%, `#6effc2`, var(--player)); box-shadow:0 0 12px rgba(0,255,153,.75), 0 0 24px rgba(0,255,153,.35) }
    .enemy{ background:radial-gradient(circle at 30% 30%, `#ff8c8c`, var(--enemy)); animation:pulse 1.2s infinite; box-shadow:0 0 12px rgba(255,0,0,.7), 0 0 24px rgba(255,0,0,.35) }
    .exit{ border-radius:6px; background:linear-gradient(180deg, `#7cc4ff`, var(--exit)); box-shadow:0 0 12px rgba(30,144,255,.85), 0 0 24px rgba(30,144,255,.45) }
    .item{ background:radial-gradient(circle at 30% 30%, `#fff5a3`, var(--item)); animation:spin 3s linear infinite }
    `@keyframes` pulse { 0%,100%{ transform:scale(1) } 50%{ transform:scale(1.12) } }
    `@keyframes` spin { from{ transform:rotate(0) } to{ transform:rotate(360deg) } }

    /* Side panel */
    .panel{ background:var(--panel); border:1px solid rgba(255,255,255,.08); border-radius:12px; padding:16px }
    .panel h2{ margin:0 0 8px; font-size:1.1rem }
    .meta{ display:grid; grid-template-columns:1fr 1fr; gap:6px 12px; font-variant-numeric:tabular-nums }
    .meta .label{ color:`#bbb`; font-size:.8rem }
    .meta .value{ font-weight:700 }
    .controls{ display:flex; gap:8px; flex-wrap:wrap; margin-top:8px }
    button{
      background:`#2a2a2a`; color:`#fff`; border:1px solid rgba(255,255,255,.15);
      border-radius:10px; padding:10px 14px; cursor:pointer; transition:.2s ease; box-shadow:0 2px 0 rgba(0,0,0,.45)
    }
    button:hover{ background:`#333`; transform:translateY(-1px) }
    button:disabled{ opacity:.5; filter:grayscale(.3); cursor:not-allowed }
    .status{ margin-top:12px; padding:10px 12px; border-radius:10px; background:rgba(255,255,255,.06); border:1px solid rgba(255,255,255,.09) }
    .legend{ display:flex; gap:10px; align-items:center; flex-wrap:wrap; margin-top:8px }
    .sample{ width:16px; height:16px; border-radius:3px; display:inline-block }
    .sample.player{ background:var(--player) }
    .sample.enemy{ background:var(--enemy) }
    .sample.item{ background:var(--item) }
    .sample.exit{ background:var(--exit) }
    .sample.wall{ background:var(--wall) }
    .sample.invis{ background:transparent; outline:1px dashed rgba(255,255,255,.25) }
    kbd{ background:`#222`; border:1px solid `#444`; border-bottom-width:3px; padding:2px 6px; border-radius:6px; font-size:.9em }

    /* Celebration overlay */
    `#overlay`{ position:absolute; inset:0; display:none; align-items:center; justify-content:center; background:radial-gradient(ellipse at center, rgba(0,0,0,.25), rgba(0,0,0,.8)); text-align:center; z-index:10 }
    `#overlay.active`{ display:flex }
    `#overlay` .content{ animation:pop 700ms cubic-bezier(.2,1,.22,1) both }
    .win-title{ font-size:clamp(28px,6vw,54px); margin:0 0 8px; text-shadow:0 4px 0 rgba(0,0,0,.55) }
    `@keyframes` pop { 0%{ transform:scale(.8); opacity:0 } 100%{ transform:scale(1); opacity:1 } }
    .confetti{ position:absolute; top:-10vh; width:8px; height:14px; opacity:.85; border-radius:2px; animation:fall 4s linear forwards }
    `@keyframes` fall{ to{ transform:translateY(120vh) rotate(720deg) } }

    /* Toast */
    `#toast`{ position:absolute; left:50%; transform:translateX(-50%); bottom:16px; background:rgba(0,0,0,.6); color:`#fff`; padding:8px 12px; border-radius:999px; border:1px solid rgba(255,255,255,.15); opacity:0; pointer-events:none; transition:opacity .25s ease }
    `#toast.show`{ opacity:1 }

    `@media` (prefers-reduced-motion:reduce){
      .enemy,.item{ animation:none }
      .confetti{ display:none }
    }
  </style>
</head>
<body>
  <div class="wrap">
    <div class="shell">
      <section id="game-area" tabindex="0" aria-label="Maze of invisible walls game area">
        <header>
          <h1 style="margin:0;font-size:1.25rem">Maze of Invisible Walls</h1>
          <p style="margin:.25rem 0 0;opacity:.85">Use arrow keys to reach the blue exit. Avoid red enemies. Invisible walls block movement until revealed.</p>
        </header>

        <div id="board" role="grid" aria-label="10 by 10 game board"></div>

        <!-- Celebration overlay -->
        <div id="overlay" role="dialog" aria-modal="true" aria-live="polite">
          <div class="content">
            <h2 class="win-title">🎉 YOU WIN! 🎉</h2>
            <p id="final-stats"></p>
            <div class="controls" style="justify-content:center;margin-top:10px">
              <button id="play-again">Play Again</button>
            </div>
          </div>
        </div>

        <div id="toast" aria-live="polite"></div>
      </section>

      <!-- Info + Controls -->
      <aside class="panel" aria-label="Game information and controls">
        <h2>Game Info</h2>
        <div class="meta">
          <div><span class="label">Level</span> <span id="ui-level" class="value">1</span></div>
          <div><span class="label">Moves</span> <span id="ui-moves" class="value">0</span></div>
          <div><span class="label">Items</span> <span id="ui-items" class="value">0</span></div>
          <div><span class="label">Status</span> <span id="ui-status" class="value">—</span></div>
        </div>
        <div class="controls">
          <button id="start">Start Game</button>
          <button id="reset" disabled>Reset Level</button>
          <button id="use-item" disabled>Use Item</button>
        </div>
        <div class="status" aria-live="polite">
          Move with <kbd>←</kbd><kbd>↑</kbd><kbd>→</kbd><kbd>↓</kbd>. Colliding with a hidden wall will reveal it. Use items to reveal all invisible walls for 3 seconds.
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
          <span class="sample player"></span> Player
          <span class="sample enemy"></span> Enemy
          <span class="sample item"></span> Item
          <span class="sample exit"></span> Exit
          <span class="sample wall"></span> Wall
          <span class="sample invis"></span> Invisible wall
        </div>
      </aside>
    </div>
  </div>

  <script>
    (() => {
      const size = 10;
      const boardEl = document.getElementById('board');
      const gameArea = document.getElementById('game-area');
      const levelEl = document.getElementById('ui-level');
      const statusEl = document.getElementById('ui-status');
      const itemsEl = document.getElementById('ui-items');
      const movesEl = document.getElementById('ui-moves');
      const btnStart = document.getElementById('start');
      const btnReset = document.getElementById('reset');
      const btnUse = document.getElementById('use-item');
      const overlay = document.getElementById('overlay');
      const finalStats = document.getElementById('final-stats');
      const playAgain = document.getElementById('play-again');
      const toast = document.getElementById('toast');

      const posKey = (x,y)=> x+','+y;
      const inBounds = (x,y)=> x>=0 && y>=0 && x<size && y<size;

      // Three progressively harder levels
      const levels = [
        {
          start:[0,0], exit:[9,9],
          walls:[[1,1],[1,2],[1,3],[2,3],[3,3],[5,0],[5,1],[5,2],[5,3],[5,4],[7,6],[7,7]],
          invis:[[2,1],[2,2],[3,2],[4,2],[4,5],[4,6],[4,7],[6,6]],
          items:[[0,6],[8,1]],
          enemies:[[3,0],[8,7]]
        },
        {
          start:[0,9], exit:[9,0],
          walls:[[2,0],[2,1],[2,2],[2,3],[3,5],[4,5],[5,5],[6,5],[6,6],[6,7],[6,8]],
          invis:[[1,7],[1,8],[1,9],[4,1],[5,1],[6,1],[7,1],[4,8],[5,8]],
          items:[[7,8],[0,4]],
          enemies:[[5,0],[7,5],[1,3]]
        },
        {
          start:[5,9], exit:[0,0],
          walls:[[8,2],[8,3],[8,4],[8,5],[3,6],[4,6],[5,6],[1,2],[1,3],[1,4]],
          invis:[[6,2],[6,3],[6,4],[2,7],[2,8],[2,9],[4,2],[5,2],[6,8],[7,8]],
          items:[[9,9],[4,9],[2,0]],
          enemies:[[6,0],[4,4],[9,2],[0,7]]
        }
      ];

      let state = {};
      let enemyTimer = null;
      let revealAllUntil = 0;

      function initLevel(index) {
        const lvl = levels[index];
        state = {
          levelIndex: index,
          player: {x:lvl.start[0], y:lvl.start[1]},
          exit: {x:lvl.exit[0], y:lvl.exit[1]},
          walls: new Set(lvl.walls.map(p=> posKey(...p))),
          invis: new Set(lvl.invis.map(p=> posKey(...p))),
          revealed: new Set(),
          items: new Set(lvl.items.map(p=> posKey(...p))),
          enemies: lvl.enemies.map(([x,y])=>({x,y})),
          moves: 0,
          itemsHeld: 0,
          running: true
        };
        revealAllUntil = 0;
        updateUI('Find the blue exit.');
        btnUse.disabled = state.itemsHeld <= 0;
        btnReset.disabled = false;
        render();
        focusBoard();
        if (enemyTimer) clearInterval(enemyTimer);
        enemyTimer = setInterval(stepEnemies, 1400);
      }

      function focusBoard(){ setTimeout(()=> gameArea.focus(), 0) }

      function updateUI(message) {
        if (message) statusEl.textContent = message;
        levelEl.textContent = state.levelIndex + 1;
        movesEl.textContent = state.moves;
        itemsEl.textContent = state.itemsHeld;
      }

      function showToast(msg, ms=900) {
        toast.textContent = msg;
        toast.classList.add('show');
        setTimeout(()=> toast.classList.remove('show'), ms);
      }

      function render() {
        const cells = [];
        for (let y=0; y<size; y++) {
          for (let x=0; x<size; x++) {
            const k = posKey(x,y);
            let classes = ['cell'];
            if (state.walls.has(k)) classes.push('wall');
            if (state.invis.has(k)) classes.push('invis');
            const reveal = state.revealed.has(k) || Date.now() < revealAllUntil;
            if (reveal && state.invis.has(k)) classes.push('revealed','reveal-glow');

            let html = `<div class="${classes.join(' ')}" role="gridcell" aria-label="cell ${x},${y}">`;
            if (state.exit.x===x && state.exit.y===y) html += `<div class="entity exit" title="Exit"></div>`;
            if (state.items.has(k)) html += `<div class="entity item" title="Item"></div>`;
            for (const e of state.enemies) { if (e.x===x && e.y===y) { html += `<div class="entity enemy" title="Enemy"></div>`; break; } }
            if (state.player.x===x && state.player.y===y) html += `<div class="entity player" title="Player"></div>`;
            html += `</div>`;
            cells.push(html);
          }
        }
        boardEl.innerHTML = cells.join('');
      }

      function canEnter(x,y) {
        if (!inBounds(x,y)) return {ok:false, reason:'edge'};
        const k = posKey(x,y);
        if (state.walls.has(k)) return {ok:false, reason:'wall'};
        if (state.invis.has(k)) return {ok:false, reason:'invis', key:k};
        for (const e of state.enemies) if (e.x===x && e.y===y) return {ok:false, reason:'enemy'};
        return {ok:true};
      }

      function movePlayer(dx,dy) {
        if (!state.running) return;
        const nx = state.player.x + dx;
        const ny = state.player.y + dy;
        const r = canEnter(nx,ny);
        let msg = null;

        if (r.ok) {
          state.player.x = nx; state.player.y = ny;
          state.moves++;
          const k = posKey(nx,ny);
          if (state.items.has(k)) {
            state.items.delete(k);
            state.itemsHeld++;
            btnUse.disabled = false;
            msg = 'Picked up an item.';
            showToast('⭐ +1');
          }
          if (state.exit.x===nx && state.exit.y===ny) { levelComplete(); return; }
          for (const e of state.enemies) if (e.x===nx && e.y===ny) { gameOver(); return; }
        } else {
          if (r.reason==='wall') { msg='A solid wall blocks your way.'; showToast('Blocked'); }
          if (r.reason==='edge') { msg='Edge of the maze.'; showToast('Edge'); }
          if (r.reason==='invis') {
            state.revealed.add(r.key);
            msg='You bumped into an invisible wall!';
            showToast('Invisible wall');
          }
        }
        updateUI(msg);
        render();
      }

      function stepEnemies() {
        if (!state.running) return;
        for (const e of state.enemies) {
          const dirs = shuffle([[1,0],[-1,0],[0,1],[0,-1]]);
          for (const [dx,dy] of dirs) {
            const nx = e.x + dx, ny = e.y + dy, k = posKey(nx,ny);
            if (!inBounds(nx,ny)) continue;
            if (state.walls.has(k)) continue;
            if (state.invis.has(k)) continue;
            if (nx===state.exit.x && ny===state.exit.y) continue;
            if (state.enemies.some(o=>o!==e && o.x===nx && o.y===ny)) continue;
            e.x = nx; e.y = ny;
            break;
          }
          if (e.x===state.player.x && e.y===state.player.y) { gameOver(); return; }
        }
        render();
      }

      function useItem() {
        if (state.itemsHeld<=0) return;
        state.itemsHeld--;
        btnUse.disabled = state.itemsHeld <= 0;
        revealAllUntil = Date.now() + 3000;
        updateUI('Invisible walls revealed for 3 seconds!');
        render();
        setTimeout(()=>render(), 3100);
      }

      function levelComplete() {
        if (state.levelIndex < levels.length - 1) {
          state.levelIndex++;
          updateUI('Level clear! Advancing...');
          initLevel(state.levelIndex);
        } else {
          winGame();
        }
      }

      function gameOver() {
        state.running = false;
        updateUI('Caught by an enemy. Press Reset Level to try again.');
        showToast('💥 Caught!');
      }

      function winGame() {
        state.running = false;
        clearInterval(enemyTimer);
        finalStats.textContent = `Completed ${levels.length} levels in ${state.moves} moves.`;
        overlay.classList.add('active');
        spawnConfetti(120);
      }

      function resetLevel(){ initLevel(state.levelIndex); updateUI('Level reset.'); }
      function startGame(){ overlay.classList.remove('active'); initLevel(0); }
      function focusStart(){ setTimeout(()=>gameArea.focus(), 0) }

      function spawnConfetti(n=80) {
        const colors=['#f94144','#f3722c','#f8961e','#f9c74f','#90be6d','#43aa8b','#577590','#8ecae6','#219ebc','#ffafcc'];
        for (let i=0;i<n;i++){
          const s=document.createElement('div');
          s.className='confetti';
          s.style.left=Math.random()*100+'vw';
          s.style.background=colors[i%colors.length];
          s.style.animationDelay=(Math.random()*1.5)+'s';
          s.style.transform=`translateY(-10vh) rotate(${Math.random()*360}deg)`;
          s.style.width=(6+Math.random()*6)+'px';
          s.style.height=(10+Math.random()*12)+'px';
          overlay.appendChild(s);
          setTimeout(()=>s.remove(), 6000);
        }
      }

      function shuffle(a){ for(let i=a.length-1;i>0;i--){ const j=Math.floor(Math.random()*(i+1)); [a[i],a[j]]=[a[j],a[i]] } return a }

      // Keyboard controls
      window.addEventListener('keydown', e=>{
        if (!['ArrowUp','ArrowDown','ArrowLeft','ArrowRight'].includes(e.key)) return;
        e.preventDefault();
        const map={ArrowUp:[0,-1],ArrowDown:[0,1],ArrowLeft:[-1,0],ArrowRight:[1,0]};
        movePlayer(...map[e.key]);
      });

      // Buttons
      document.getElementById('start').addEventListener('click', ()=>{ startGame(); focusStart(); });
      document.getElementById('reset').addEventListener('click', ()=>{ resetLevel(); focusStart(); });
      document.getElementById('use-item').addEventListener('click', ()=>{ useItem(); focusStart(); });
      document.getElementById('play-again').addEventListener('click', ()=>{ startGame(); focusStart(); });

      // Initial UI
      updateUI('Press Start Game to begin.');
    })();
  </script>
</body>
</html>
Notes

Central game area uses a dark red background (#8b0000) and white text, per your spec.
The 10×10 board supports players, enemies, items, visible walls, and invisible walls that reveal on bump or when using an item (3 seconds).
Info panel shows Level, Status, Items, and Moves in real time.
Controls: Start Game, Reset Level, Use Item (auto-disabled when no items).
End of the final level triggers an animated celebration overlay with confetti and a Play Again button.
If you’d like, I can package this into your repo as game/maze_invisible_walls.html in a follow-up PR—just say “plan code changes” and I’ll prepare the steps.

NVIDIA's AI Pivot Narrative.docx

User: Help me map how NVIDIA quietly turned itself from a graphics-card company into the gatekeeper of the AI boom.
671.6Hz
Start by tracing the pivot points: the first big data-center win, the moment when gamers couldn’t buy a card because miners snapped them up, and the handshake deals that put A100s into every cloud region. I want to see how each of those moves fed the next—more compute sold means more software locks in CUDA, which means more future compute sold. Then stack that against the competitive set: where AMD and Intel still have silicon leverage, where startups are trying to knife in with specialty chips, and where hyperscalers building their own silicon could still blunt NVIDIA’s margin.
Keep an eye on regulatory smoke: export controls, antitrust chatter, and the weird geopolitics of fabs. If TSMC hiccups or Uncle Sam tightens the China choke-chain again, the whole roadmap wobbles.
Deliver it as a single-scroll narrative page:
• Hero section: a dark, star-field GPU die shot that slowly morphs into a glowing neural-network lattice—visually hinting that the same silicon art now powers both Fortnite and foundation models.
Kimi: Here is the single-scroll narrative page mapping NVIDIA's quiet transformation from a graphics-card company into the gatekeeper of the AI boom.

<!-- Hero Section -->
<section class="hero">
    <canvas class="hero-canvas" id="heroCanvas"></canvas>
    <div class="hero-content">
        <h1>The Silicon Pivot</h1>
        <p class="hero-subtitle">How NVIDIA quietly turned itself from a graphics-card company into the gatekeeper of the AI boom</p>
        <div class="hero-meta">
            <span>From Fortnite to Foundation Models</span>
            <span>•</span>
            <span>2006 — 2026</span>
        </div>
    </div>
    <div class="scroll-indicator">↓</div>
</section>

<!-- Introduction -->
<div class="section">
    <p class="lead">In 2012, a University of Toronto grad student named Alex Krizhevsky trained a neural network on two NVIDIA GTX 580 GPUs in his bedroom and crushed the ImageNet competition. That moment—AlexNet—didn't just win a computer vision contest. It revealed that the same silicon art powering <em>Fortnite</em> could simulate human intelligence. NVIDIA's market cap was under $10 billion then. Today it sits north of $3 trillion. This is the story of how that happened.</p>
</div>

<div class="section-divider"></div>

<!-- Part 1: The Pivot Points -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>I. The Pivot Points</h2>
    
    <h3>1. CUDA: The Developer Capture (2006)</h3>
    <p>In 2006, NVIDIA introduced CUDA—the Compute Unified Device Architecture—a parallel computing platform that let developers run general-purpose code on GPUs. At the time, this was a bet on scientific computing and simulation. What it actually did was create a software ecosystem with switching costs that analysts now estimate at <strong>6–12 months of engineering effort</strong> for large-scale users to migrate away from.</p>
    
    <p>By the time deep learning exploded in the 2010s, PyTorch and TensorFlow had been built with CUDA as the preferred backend. Every optimized kernel, every research paper's code, every startup's model—locked to NVIDIA's execution model. AMD's ROCm and OpenCL faced a causality dilemma: underperformance meant no incentive to write more kernels, which meant more underperformance.</p>

    <div class="quote-block">
        "In 2009, I remember giving a talk at NIPS where I told about 1,000 researchers they should all buy GPUs because GPUs are going to be the future of machine learning."
        <div class="quote-attrib">— Geoffrey Hinton</div>
    </div>

    <h3>2. AlexNet: The First Data-Center Win (2012)</h3>
    <p>AlexNet's victory at ImageNet in October 2012 was the inflection. Krizhevsky's network had 60 million parameters—1,000x larger than LeCun's 1998 nets—and trained on two consumer GTX 580s. The AI research community noticed immediately. By 2015, Google, Microsoft, and Baidu were all achieving superhuman perception on NVIDIA hardware.</p>
    
    <p>NVIDIA leaned in. In 2016, Jensen Huang donated the first DGX-1 AI supercomputer—eight GPUs in a box—to OpenAI. The DGX line became the template for modern AI infrastructure.</p>

    <h3>3. The Crypto Gold Rush (2017 & 2021)</h3>
    <p>Here's where the narrative gets interesting. The same parallel compute that made GPUs perfect for AI also made them perfect for cryptocurrency mining. In 2017, Ethereum miners bought up every GeForce card they could find. Gamers couldn't buy an RTX 3080 at MSRP for nearly two years.</p>
    
    <p>NVIDIA's response was telling: they launched the CMP (Cryptocurrency Mining Processor) line—dedicated mining cards with no video outputs—and implemented "Lite Hash Rate" (LHR) limiters on gaming GPUs. In Q1 2021 alone, CMP sales hit $155 million. But the real signal was what this demand proved: NVIDIA's silicon was the universal compute substrate. Whether you were mining crypto or training transformers, you needed their chips.</p>

    <div class="stats-grid">
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">700K</span>
            <div class="stat-label">GPUs shipped to miners in Q1 2021</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">25%</span>
            <div class="stat-label">of all GPUs went to miners that quarter</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">$500M</span>
            <div class="stat-label">Estimated mining GPU market value</div>
        </div>
    </div>

    <h3>4. The Cloud Handshake (2020–2021)</h3>
    <p>The A100—NVIDIA's first data-center-native Ampere GPU—became the universal cloud currency. AWS launched P4 instances in September 2020. Oracle followed. Google Cloud's A2 VMs went GA in March 2021, offering up to 16 A100s in a single VM—the largest single-node GPU instance from any major provider. Microsoft Azure's ND A100 v4 series brought 200 Gbps InfiniBand interconnects.</p>
    
    <p>These weren't just product launches. They were structural lock-ins. Every cloud region that deployed A100s was committing to NVIDIA's ecosystem: CUDA, NVLink, InfiniBand, and eventually the full DGX stack. Cloud providers became NVIDIA's distribution channel, and NVIDIA became the compute layer of the internet.</p>

    <div class="timeline">
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">Sep 2020</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">AWS P4 Instances Go Live</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">First major cloud A100 deployment, up to 8 GPUs per instance</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">Nov 2020</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Oracle Cloud A100 GA</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">Bare-metal A100 instances with full machine access</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">Mar 2021</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Google Cloud A2 VMs GA</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">Up to 16 A100 GPUs per VM—largest single-node offering</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2022</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Azure ND A100 v4 Series</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">200 Gbps InfiniBand, integrated with Azure ML ecosystem</div>
        </div>
    </div>
</div>

<div class="section-divider"></div>

<!-- Part 2: The Flywheel -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>II. The Flywheel: Compute → CUDA → More Compute</h2>
    
    <p class="lead">NVIDIA's dominance isn't just about making better chips. It's about a self-reinforcing cycle that gets stronger with every GPU sold.</p>

    <div class="flywheel">
        <div class="flywheel-step">
            <strong>More Compute Sold</strong>
            Every A100/H100/Blackwell that ships into a data center becomes the platform developers write code for
        </div>
        <div class="flywheel-step">
            <strong>More Software Locks In</strong>
            CUDA kernels, TensorRT optimizations, NVLink-aware distributed training—all tied to NVIDIA hardware
        </div>
        <div class="flywheel-step">
            <strong>Higher Switching Costs</strong>
            Migrating to AMD or Intel means rewriting months of optimized code, retraining teams, retooling pipelines
        </div>
        <div class="flywheel-step">
            <strong>More Future Compute Sold</strong>
            Next-gen buyers default to NVIDIA because their stack, their talent, and their models are already optimized for it
        </div>
    </div>

    <p>This is why NVIDIA's gross margins sit at <strong>75%</strong>—unheard of for a hardware company. They're not selling commodity silicon. They're selling a platform with a 20-year head start on software optimization.</p>

    <div class="revenue-visual">
        <h3 style="margin-top: 0; color: #fff;">The Revenue Flip</h3>
        <p style="color: var(--text-secondary); font-size: 0.9rem;">Gaming vs. Data Center revenue share</p>
        <div class="bar-chart">
            <div class="bar-group">
                <div style="display: flex; width: 100%; flex-direction: column; gap: 2px;">
                    <div class="bar datacenter" style="height: 50px;"><span class="bar-value">$655M</span></div>

    </div>
</div>

<div class="section-divider"></div>

<!-- Part 3: Competitive Landscape -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>III. The Competitive Set</h2>
    
    <p class="lead">NVIDIA holds 80–90% of the AI accelerator market. But the remaining 10–20% is where the most interesting battles are being fought.</p>

    <div class="competitor-card amd">
        <div class="competitor-name">AMD: The Silicon Challenger</div>
        <p>The MI300X is AMD's best shot. With <strong>192GB of HBM3</strong> memory, it surpasses the H100's 80GB—critical for large language model inference. Microsoft has deployed MI300X in Azure for OpenAI workloads. Meta standardized on it for Llama 3.1 inference. Oracle is building AI clusters around it.</p>
        <p>But AMD's software ecosystem—ROCm—still lags CUDA in usability and optimization breadth. The hardware is competitive; the developer experience isn't. AMD projects AI accelerator revenue of ~$7B in 2025, a fraction of NVIDIA's ~$120B+ data center run rate.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="competitor-card intel">
        <div class="competitor-name">Intel: The Cost Play</div>
        <p>Gaudi 3 is Intel's answer, positioned as <strong>50% cheaper</strong> than H100 with competitive performance-per-watt. The pitch is enterprise AI—companies that want AI acceleration without the NVIDIA tax. But Gaudi isn't a GPU; it's a dedicated AI accelerator with a different programming model. That architectural difference is a hurdle most developers won't cross unless the price delta is overwhelming.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="competitor-card hyperscaler">
        <div class="competitor-name">Hyperscalers: Building Their Own Silicon</div>
        <p>Google's TPUs (now Ironwood/v7), Amazon's Trainium3, Microsoft's Maia—these are the real long-term threats. Not because any one of them will dethrone NVIDIA, but because they represent a multi-vendor strategy that reduces dependency.</p>
        <p>Anthropic runs a tri-platform setup: Google TPU, AWS Trainium, and NVIDIA GPUs in parallel. OpenAI signed a TPU deal for inference workloads in 2025. Meta signed a multi-billion-dollar TPU contract for Llama 4. The logic is diversification and price leverage.</p>
        <p>But here's the catch: <strong>everyone is competing for TSMC slots</strong>. TSMC allocated 28% of its total wafer capacity to AI chips in 2025, with 3nm and 5nm nodes accounting for 74% of wafer revenue. NVIDIA gets the best slots because it writes the biggest upfront checks, its chips command the highest revenue-per-wafer, and Jensen Huang's three-decade relationship with TSMC founder Morris Chang still matters.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="stats-grid">
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">90%+</span>
            <div class="stat-label">NVIDIA AI GPU market share</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">~$7B</span>
            <div class="stat-label">AMD 2025 AI revenue forecast</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">$1B+</span>
            <div class="stat-label">Intel Gaudi 2024 revenue target</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">28%</span>
            <div class="stat-label">TSMC wafer capacity to AI chips</div>
        </div>
    </div>
</div>

<div class="section-divider"></div>

<!-- Part 4: Regulatory Smoke -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>IV. Regulatory Smoke & Geopolitics</h2>
    
    <h3>Export Controls: The China Choke-Chain</h3>
    <p>Since 2022, the U.S. has implemented a fluctuating export control regime to bar China from obtaining the most advanced AI chips. NVIDIA designed the H20 specifically to comply with these rules—only to have the U.S. impose new licensing requirements in April 2025 that forced NVIDIA to take a <strong>$5.5 billion earnings hit</strong>.</p>
    
    <p>Jensen Huang has been explicit: China's AI market could be worth $50 billion, and losing access is a "tremendous loss." By July 2025, NVIDIA had received export assurances and was preparing to sell H20s in China again. But the whiplash illustrates the core risk: NVIDIA's revenue is increasingly hostage to geopolitical winds.</p>

    <h3>Antitrust Chatter</h3>
    <p>In September 2024, the U.S. Department of Justice escalated scrutiny by sending NVIDIA a subpoena, seeking evidence of antitrust violations. Officials were concerned that NVIDIA makes it harder to switch to other suppliers and penalizes buyers who don't exclusively use its GPUs. The UK Competition and Markets Authority identified an "interconnected web" of over 90 partnerships and strategic investments involving the same firms: Google, Apple, Microsoft, Meta, Amazon, and NVIDIA.</p>
    
    <p>China's State Administration for Market Regulation (SAMR) launched its own probe in December 2024, investigating whether NVIDIA violated commitments made during its 2020 Mellanox acquisition. In September 2025, SAMR concluded that NVIDIA had violated anti-monopoly laws.</p>

    <h3>The TSMC Bottleneck</h3>
    <p>TSMC is the real gatekeeper. Over 90% of the most efficient AI chips are produced by TSMC in Taiwan, using EUV lithography equipment supplied only by ASML in the Netherlands. If TSMC hiccups—earthquake, geopolitical conflict, power grid failure—the entire AI industry's roadmap wobbles.</p>
    
    <p>TSMC is building in Arizona: Fab 21 Phase 1 is already producing 4nm chips for Apple and NVIDIA. Phase 2 will do 3nm by 2027. But the advanced packaging facility (CoWoS) needed for AI chip integration won't be online until 2028. Until then, the most critical step in making an AI accelerator still happens in Taiwan.</p>

    <div class="warning-box">
        <h4>The Single Point of Failure</h4>
        <p>NVIDIA doesn't control its own manufacturing. TSMC does. And TSMC's capacity is oversubscribed by 3x. Some customers are paying 50–100% premiums for "hot run" priority. If geopolitics disrupts Taiwan operations, there is no near-term alternative. The $165 billion Arizona expansion is insurance—but insurance that won't fully pay out for years.</p>
    </div>
</div>

<div class="section-divider"></div>

<!-- Part 5: The Roadmap -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>V. The Roadmap: Blackwell to Rubin to Feynman</h2>
    
    <p>NVIDIA has accelerated from a biennial to a <strong>yearly release cadence</strong>. This isn't just about performance—it's about making competitive hardware obsolete before it can gain traction.</p>

    <div class="timeline">
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2024</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Blackwell Architecture</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">20 petaflops FP4, 192GB HBM3e. Already shipped $11B in revenue. Top 4 buyers purchased 1.8M chips.</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2025</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Blackwell Ultra</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">288GB HBM3e, 1.5x performance. 1.1 exaflops per rack.</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2026</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Vera Rubin</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">3nm process, HBM4 memory, 50 petaflops FP4. 3.6 exaflops per rack. Custom "Olympus" ARM cores.</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2027</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Rubin Ultra</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">15 exaflops per rack, 1TB memory. 13.6x performance increase over Blackwell Ultra in just two years.</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2028</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Feynman Architecture</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">Next-gen after Rubin. Projected 30x+ performance over Blackwell Ultra.</div>
        </div>
    </div>

    <p>The "Vera Rubin Superchip" pairs the Rubin GPU with NVIDIA's own Vera CPU, connected via NVLink C2C at 1,800 GB/s. This is vertical integration on a scale that makes Apple's silicon strategy look modest. NVIDIA isn't just selling GPUs anymore—it's selling <strong>AI factories in a box</strong>.</p>
</div>

<div class="section-divider"></div>

<!-- Conclusion -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>VI. The Gatekeeper Thesis</h2>
    
    <p class="lead">NVIDIA's transformation from graphics company to AI gatekeeper wasn't a single decision. It was a sequence of compounding bets: CUDA in 2006, AlexNet validation in 2012, the crypto stress-test in 2017 and 2021, and the cloud handshake deals of 2020–2021 that put A100s into every major region.</p>
    
    <p>Each phase fed the next. Crypto proved the silicon could handle arbitrary parallel workloads at scale. The cloud deals created the distribution infrastructure. And CUDA ensured that every developer who learned AI on NVIDIA hardware would demand NVIDIA hardware for their next project.</p>
    
    <p>The competitive threats are real—AMD has silicon leverage, hyperscalers have vertical integration incentives, and startups are carving out inference niches. But NVIDIA's response is to accelerate its roadmap so aggressively that by the time a competitor ships hardware matching today's flagship, NVIDIA has already moved two generations ahead.</p>
    
    <p>The real risk isn't competition. It's concentration. TSMC's Taiwan fabs, U.S. export controls, antitrust probes in three jurisdictions, and the sheer physics of power and cooling at gigawatt scale—these are the forces that could actually slow the machine. NVIDIA doesn't just make the best AI chips. It has become the infrastructure layer of the AI era. And infrastructure, by definition, is hard to replace.</p>

    <div class="stats-grid" style="margin-top: 3rem;">
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">$216B</span>
            <div class="stat-label">NVIDIA FY2026 annual revenue</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">91%</span>
            <div class="stat-label">Data center share of revenue</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">75%</span>
            <div class="stat-label">Gross margin</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">$1T</span>
            <div class="stat-label">Projected Blackwell + Rubin sales through 2027</div>
        </div>
    </div>
</div>

    <p>Data compiled from NVIDIA SEC filings, earnings calls, TSMC disclosures, and industry analysis.</p>
    <p style="margin-top: 0.5rem; opacity: 0.6;">The same silicon art now powers both Fortnite and foundation models.</p>
</div>

<script>
// Hero Canvas Animation - GPU Die Shot morphing into Neural Network Lattice
const canvas = document.getElementById('heroCanvas');
const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');

let width, height;
let particles = [];
let morphProgress = 0;
let morphDirection = 1;
let time = 0;

function resize() {
    width = canvas.width = window.innerWidth;
    height = canvas.height = window.innerHeight;
    initParticles();
}

class Particle {
    constructor(x, y, type) {
        this.x = x;
        this.y = y;
        this.targetX = x;
        this.targetY = y;
        this.size = Math.random() * 2 + 0.5;
        this.baseSize = this.size;
        this.type = type; // 'die' or 'neuron'
        this.connections = [];
        this.brightness = Math.random() * 0.5 + 0.2;
        this.pulse = Math.random() * Math.PI * 2;
    }

    update() {
        this.pulse += 0.02;
        
        // Subtle floating movement
        this.x += Math.sin(time * 0.5 + this.pulse) * 0.2;
        this.y += Math.cos(time * 0.3 + this.pulse) * 0.2;

        // Size pulsing
        this.size = this.baseSize * (1 + Math.sin(this.pulse) * 0.3);
    }

    draw() {
        const alpha = this.brightness * (0.5 + Math.sin(this.pulse) * 0.5);
        
        if (this.type === 'die') {
            // GPU die shot style - grid-like, rectangular
            ctx.fillStyle = `rgba(100, 160, 255, ${alpha * 0.8})`;
            ctx.fillRect(this.x - this.size, this.y - this.size, this.size * 2, this.size * 2);
        } else {
            // Neural network style - circular, glowing
            const gradient = ctx.createRadialGradient(this.x, this.y, 0, this.x, this.y, this.size * 3);
            gradient.addColorStop(0, `rgba(118, 185, 0, ${alpha})`);
            gradient.addColorStop(0.5, `rgba(118, 185, 0, ${alpha * 0.3})`);
            gradient.addColorStop(1, 'rgba(118, 185, 0, 0)');
            ctx.fillStyle = gradient;
            ctx.beginPath();
            ctx.arc(this.x, this.y, this.size * 3, 0, Math.PI * 2);
            ctx.fill();
        }
    }
}

function initParticles() {
    particles = [];
    const count = Math.min(400, Math.floor((width * height) / 4000));
    
    for (let i = 0; i < count; i++) {
        const x = Math.random() * width;
        const y = Math.random() * height;
        particles.push(new Particle(x, y, Math.random() > 0.5 ? 'die' : 'neuron'));
    }
}

function drawConnections() {
    const maxDist = 150;
    const maxConnections = 3;
    
    for (let i = 0; i < particles.length; i++) {
        let connections = 0;
        for (let j = i + 1; j < particles.length; j++) {
            const dx = particles[i].x - particles[j].x;
            const dy = particles[i].y - particles[j].y;
            const dist = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy);
            
            if (dist < maxDist && connections < maxConnections) {
                const alpha = (1 - dist / maxDist) * 0.15;
                
                if (particles[i].type === 'neuron' && particles[j].type === 'neuron') {
                    // Neural connections - organic curves
                    ctx.strokeStyle = `rgba(118, 185, 0, ${alpha})`;
                    ctx.lineWidth = 0.5;
                    ctx.beginPath();
                    ctx.moveTo(particles[i].x, particles[i].y);
                    const cx = (particles[i].x + particles[j].x) / 2 + Math.sin(time + i) * 20;
                    const cy = (particles[i].y + particles[j].y) / 2 + Math.cos(time + j) * 20;
                    ctx.quadraticCurveTo(cx, cy, particles[j].x, particles[j].y);
                    ctx.stroke();
                } else if (particles[i].type === 'die' && particles[j].type === 'die') {
                    // Die connections - straight grid lines
                    ctx.strokeStyle = `rgba(100, 160, 255, ${alpha * 0.5})`;
                    ctx.lineWidth = 0.3;
                    ctx.beginPath();
                    ctx.moveTo(particles[i].x, particles[i].y);
                    ctx.lineTo(particles[j].x, particles[j].y);
                    ctx.stroke();
                }
                
                connections++;
            }
        }
    }
}

function animate() {
    ctx.fillStyle = 'rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.05)';
    ctx.fillRect(0, 0, width, height);
    
    time += 0.01;
    
    // Morph between die and neuron patterns
    morphProgress += 0.002 * morphDirection;
    if (morphProgress > 1 || morphProgress < 0) morphDirection *= -1;
    
    // Update particle types based on morph
    particles.forEach((p, i) => {
        // Create a wave-like morph pattern
        const wave = Math.sin(time * 0.5 + i * 0.05) * 0.5 + 0.5;
        p.type = wave > morphProgress ? 'neuron' : 'die';
        p.update();
        p.draw();
    });
    
    drawConnections();
    
    // Central glow
    const centerGradient = ctx.createRadialGradient(width/2, height/2, 0, width/2, height/2, Math.min(width, height) * 0.4);
    centerGradient.addColorStop(0, `rgba(118, 185, 0, ${0.03 + Math.sin(time) * 0.01})`);
    centerGradient.addColorStop(0.5, `rgba(100, 160, 255, ${0.02 + Math.cos(time) * 0.01})`);
    centerGradient.addColorStop(1, 'transparent');
    ctx.fillStyle = centerGradient;
    ctx.fillRect(0, 0, width, height);
    
    requestAnimationFrame(animate);
}

window.addEventListener('resize', resize);
resize();
animate();

// Parallax effect on scroll
window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
    const scrolled = window.pageYOffset;
    const hero = document.querySelector('.hero-content');
    if (hero && scrolled < window.innerHeight) {
        hero.style.transform = `translateY(${scrolled * 0.3}px)`;
        hero.style.opacity = 1 - (scrolled / window.innerHeight);
    }
});
</script>

</body>
</html>

Contributor
@mohammadyounus128198-cyber, the Kimi-generated narrative page is visually compelling and structurally sound. Here's a precise technical audit of the Canvas animation and page mechanics:

🔍 Code Review: NVIDIA Pivot Narrative Page
🔴 Issue 1 — Particles Permanently Drift Off-Screen
this.x += Math.sin(time * 0.5 + this.pulse) * 0.2;
this.y += Math.cos(time * 0.3 + this.pulse) * 0.2;
These accumulate unboundedly. After a few minutes, all particles wander out of the viewport. The trail effect (fillRect with 5% alpha) only helps visually — it doesn't reposition particles.

Fix: Wrap coordinates back into bounds:

this.x = ((this.x + Math.sin(time * 0.5 + this.pulse) * 0.2) + width) % width;
this.y = ((this.y + Math.cos(time * 0.3 + this.pulse) * 0.2) + height) % height;
🔴 Issue 2 — O(n²) Connection Loop at 60fps
for (let i = 0; i < particles.length; i++) {
  for (let j = i + 1; j < particles.length; j++) { // up to 79,800 checks/frame at 400 particles
At 400 particles × 60fps = ~4.8M distance calculations per second. On mobile this will cause dropped frames.

Fix: Spatial bucketing (divide canvas into a grid, only check adjacent cells) or simply cap particles lower on mobile:

const isMobile = window.innerWidth < 768;
const count = Math.min(isMobile ? 100 : 400, Math.floor((width * height) / 4000));
🔴 Issue 3 — Resize Spawns Duplicate Animation Loops
resize() calls initParticles() but never cancels the existing requestAnimationFrame loop. Each resize event spawns a new animate() chain running in parallel.

Fix:

let rafId;

function animate() {
  // ... existing logic
  rafId = requestAnimationFrame(animate);
}

function resize() {
  width = canvas.width = window.innerWidth;
  height = canvas.height = window.innerHeight;
  cancelAnimationFrame(rafId);  // stop old loop
  initParticles();
  rafId = requestAnimationFrame(animate);  // start fresh
}
🟡 Issue 4 — pageYOffset Deprecated + Non-Passive Scroll Listener
const scrolled = window.pageYOffset;  // deprecated
window.addEventListener('scroll', () => { ... });  // blocks compositor
Fix:

window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
  const scrolled = window.scrollY;  // use scrollY
  // ...
}, { passive: true });  // passive: true prevents jank warning
🟡 Issue 5 — morphProgress Overshoots Boundary
morphProgress += 0.002 * morphDirection;
if (morphProgress > 1 || morphProgress < 0) morphDirection *= -1;
The check runs after the increment, so morphProgress can reach ~1.002 or ~-0.002 before clamping. Minor but causes a visible flicker at the morph boundary.

Fix:

morphProgress = Math.max(0, Math.min(1, morphProgress + 0.002 * morphDirection));
if (morphProgress >= 1 || morphProgress <= 0) morphDirection *= -1;
⚪ Issue 6 — Bar Chart Is Not Accessible
The revenue comparison chart uses CSS height values for data encoding with no aria-label or structured data. Screen readers see nothing meaningful.

Fix: Add aria-label to each bar group:

<div class="bar datacenter" style="height: 400px;" 
     aria-label="Data Center revenue $62.3 billion, 91% of total"></div>
✅ Summary Table
Issue	Severity	Fix
Particles drift off-screen over time	🔴 Bug	Wrap with modulo
O(n²) connection loop at 60fps	🔴 Perf	Spatial bucketing or particle cap
Resize spawns duplicate RAF loops	🔴 Bug	Cancel RAF before reinit
pageYOffset deprecated + non-passive scroll	🟡 Compat	scrollY + { passive: true }
morphProgress boundary overshoot	🟡 Visual	Clamp before flip
Bar chart inaccessible to screen readers	⚪ A11y	aria-label on bars
The narrative content and visual design are excellent — these are implementation-layer fixes that will make the animation robust for long sessions and mobile browsers. If you want these applied to the file already committed at apps/web/public/maze_invisible_walls.html or a new file, say "plan code changes" and I'll prepare the diff.

<!-- Introduction -->
<div class="section">
    <p class="lead">In 2012, a University of Toronto grad student named Alex Krizhevsky trained a neural network on two NVIDIA GTX 580 GPUs in his bedroom and crushed the ImageNet competition. That moment—AlexNet—didn't just win a computer vision contest. It revealed that the same silicon art powering <em>Fortnite</em> could simulate human intelligence. NVIDIA's market cap was under $10 billion then. Today it sits north of $3 trillion. This is the story of how that happened.</p>
</div>

<div class="section-divider"></div>

<!-- Part 1: The Pivot Points -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>I. The Pivot Points</h2>
    
    <h3>1. CUDA: The Developer Capture (2006)</h3>
    <p>In 2006, NVIDIA introduced CUDA—the Compute Unified Device Architecture—a parallel computing platform that let developers run general-purpose code on GPUs. At the time, this was a bet on scientific computing and simulation. What it actually did was create a software ecosystem with switching costs that analysts now estimate at <strong>6–12 months of engineering effort</strong> for large-scale users to migrate away from.</p>
    
    <p>By the time deep learning exploded in the 2010s, PyTorch and TensorFlow had been built with CUDA as the preferred backend. Every optimized kernel, every research paper's code, every startup's model—locked to NVIDIA's execution model. AMD's ROCm and OpenCL faced a causality dilemma: underperformance meant no incentive to write more kernels, which meant more underperformance.</p>

    <div class="quote-block">
        "In 2009, I remember giving a talk at NIPS where I told about 1,000 researchers they should all buy GPUs because GPUs are going to be the future of machine learning."
        <div class="quote-attrib">— Geoffrey Hinton</div>
    </div>

    <h3>2. AlexNet: The First Data-Center Win (2012)</h3>
    <p>AlexNet's victory at ImageNet in October 2012 was the inflection. Krizhevsky's network had 60 million parameters—1,000x larger than LeCun's 1998 nets—and trained on two consumer GTX 580s. The AI research community noticed immediately. By 2015, Google, Microsoft, and Baidu were all achieving superhuman perception on NVIDIA hardware.</p>
    
    <p>NVIDIA leaned in. In 2016, Jensen Huang donated the first DGX-1 AI supercomputer—eight GPUs in a box—to OpenAI. The DGX line became the template for modern AI infrastructure.</p>

    <h3>3. The Crypto Gold Rush (2017 & 2021)</h3>
    <p>Here's where the narrative gets interesting. The same parallel compute that made GPUs perfect for AI also made them perfect for cryptocurrency mining. In 2017, Ethereum miners bought up every GeForce card they could find. Gamers couldn't buy an RTX 3080 at MSRP for nearly two years.</p>
    
    <p>NVIDIA's response was telling: they launched the CMP (Cryptocurrency Mining Processor) line—dedicated mining cards with no video outputs—and implemented "Lite Hash Rate" (LHR) limiters on gaming GPUs. In Q1 2021 alone, CMP sales hit $155 million. But the real signal was what this demand proved: NVIDIA's silicon was the universal compute substrate. Whether you were mining crypto or training transformers, you needed their chips.</p>

    <div class="stats-grid">
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">700K</span>
            <div class="stat-label">GPUs shipped to miners in Q1 2021</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">25%</span>
            <div class="stat-label">of all GPUs went to miners that quarter</div>
        </div>
        <div class="stat-card">
            <span class="stat-number">$500M</span>
            <div class="stat-label">Estimated mining GPU market value</div>
        </div>
    </div>

    <h3>4. The Cloud Handshake (2020–2021)</h3>
    <p>The A100—NVIDIA's first data-center-native Ampere GPU—became the universal cloud currency. AWS launched P4 instances in September 2020. Oracle followed. Google Cloud's A2 VMs went GA in March 2021, offering up to 16 A100s in a single VM—the largest single-node GPU instance from any major provider. Microsoft Azure's ND A100 v4 series brought 200 Gbps InfiniBand interconnects.</p>
    
    <p>These weren't just product launches. They were structural lock-ins. Every cloud region that deployed A100s was committing to NVIDIA's ecosystem: CUDA, NVLink, InfiniBand, and eventually the full DGX stack. Cloud providers became NVIDIA's distribution channel, and NVIDIA became the compute layer of the internet.</p>

    <div class="timeline">
        <div class="timeline-item">

<!-- Part 2: The Flywheel -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>II. The Flywheel: Compute → CUDA → More Compute</h2>
    
    <p class="lead">NVIDIA's dominance isn't just about making better chips. It's about a self-reinforcing cycle that gets stronger with every GPU sold.</p>

    <div class="flywheel">
        <div class="flywheel-step">
            <strong>More Compute Sold</strong>
            Every A100/H100/Blackwell that ships into a data center becomes the platform developers write code for
        </div>
        <div class="flywheel-step">
            <strong>More Software Locks In</strong>
            CUDA kernels, TensorRT optimizations, NVLink-aware distributed training—all tied to NVIDIA hardware
        </div>
        <div class="flywheel-step">
            <strong>Higher Switching Costs</strong>
            Migrating to AMD or Intel means rewriting months of optimized code, retraining teams, retooling pipelines
        </div>
        <div class="flywheel-step">
            <strong>More Future Compute Sold</strong>
            Next-gen buyers default to NVIDIA because their stack, their talent, and their models are already optimized for it
        </div>
    </div>

    <p>This is why NVIDIA's gross margins sit at <strong>75%</strong>—unheard of for a hardware company. They're not selling commodity silicon. They're selling a platform with a 20-year head start on software optimization.</p>

    <div class="revenue-visual">

<!-- Part 3: Competitive Landscape -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>III. The Competitive Set</h2>
    
    <p class="lead">NVIDIA holds 80–90% of the AI accelerator market. But the remaining 10–20% is where the most interesting battles are being fought.</p>

    <div class="competitor-card amd">
        <div class="competitor-name">AMD: The Silicon Challenger</div>
        <p>The MI300X is AMD's best shot. With <strong>192GB of HBM3</strong> memory, it surpasses the H100's 80GB—critical for large language model inference. Microsoft has deployed MI300X in Azure for OpenAI workloads. Meta standardized on it for Llama 3.1 inference. Oracle is building AI clusters around it.</p>
        <p>But AMD's software ecosystem—ROCm—still lags CUDA in usability and optimization breadth. The hardware is competitive; the developer experience isn't. AMD projects AI accelerator revenue of ~$7B in 2025, a fraction of NVIDIA's ~$120B+ data center run rate.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="competitor-card intel">
        <div class="competitor-name">Intel: The Cost Play</div>
        <p>Gaudi 3 is Intel's answer, positioned as <strong>50% cheaper</strong> than H100 with competitive performance-per-watt. The pitch is enterprise AI—companies that want AI acceleration without the NVIDIA tax. But Gaudi isn't a GPU; it's a dedicated AI accelerator with a different programming model. That architectural difference is a hurdle most developers won't cross unless the price delta is overwhelming.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="competitor-card hyperscaler">
        <div class="competitor-name">Hyperscalers: Building Their Own Silicon</div>
        <p>Google's TPUs (now Ironwood/v7), Amazon's Trainium3, Microsoft's Maia—these are the real long-term threats. Not because any one of them will dethrone NVIDIA, but because they represent a multi-vendor strategy that reduces dependency.</p>
        <p>Anthropic runs a tri-platform setup: Google TPU, AWS Trainium, and NVIDIA GPUs in parallel. OpenAI signed a TPU deal for inference workloads in 2025. Meta signed a multi-billion-dollar TPU contract for Llama 4. The logic is diversification and price leverage.</p>
        <p>But here's the catch: <strong>everyone is competing for TSMC slots</strong>. TSMC allocated 28% of its total wafer capacity to AI chips in 2025, with 3nm and 5nm nodes accounting for 74% of wafer revenue. NVIDIA gets the best slots because it writes the biggest upfront checks, its chips command the highest revenue-per-wafer, and Jensen Huang's three-decade relationship with TSMC founder Morris Chang still matters.</p>
    </div>

<!-- Part 4: Regulatory Smoke -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>IV. Regulatory Smoke & Geopolitics</h2>
    
    <h3>Export Controls: The China Choke-Chain</h3>
    <p>Since 2022, the U.S. has implemented a fluctuating export control regime to bar China from obtaining the most advanced AI chips. NVIDIA designed the H20 specifically to comply with these rules—only to have the U.S. impose new licensing requirements in April 2025 that forced NVIDIA to take a <strong>$5.5 billion earnings hit</strong>.</p>
    
    <p>Jensen Huang has been explicit: China's AI market could be worth $50 billion, and losing access is a "tremendous loss." By July 2025, NVIDIA had received export assurances and was preparing to sell H20s in China again. But the whiplash illustrates the core risk: NVIDIA's revenue is increasingly hostage to geopolitical winds.</p>

    <h3>Antitrust Chatter</h3>
    <p>In September 2024, the U.S. Department of Justice escalated scrutiny by sending NVIDIA a subpoena, seeking evidence of antitrust violations. Officials were concerned that NVIDIA makes it harder to switch to other suppliers and penalizes buyers who don't exclusively use its GPUs. The UK Competition and Markets Authority identified an "interconnected web" of over 90 partnerships and strategic investments involving the same firms: Google, Apple, Microsoft, Meta, Amazon, and NVIDIA.</p>
    
    <p>China's State Administration for Market Regulation (SAMR) launched its own probe in December 2024, investigating whether NVIDIA violated commitments made during its 2020 Mellanox acquisition. In September 2025, SAMR concluded that NVIDIA had violated anti-monopoly laws.</p>

    <h3>The TSMC Bottleneck</h3>
    <p>TSMC is the real gatekeeper. Over 90% of the most efficient AI chips are produced by TSMC in Taiwan, using EUV lithography equipment supplied only by ASML in the Netherlands. If TSMC hiccups—earthquake, geopolitical conflict, power grid failure—the entire AI industry's roadmap wobbles.</p>
    
    <p>TSMC is building in Arizona: Fab 21 Phase 1 is already producing 4nm chips for Apple and NVIDIA. Phase 2 will do 3nm by 2027. But the advanced packaging facility (CoWoS) needed for AI chip integration won't be online until 2028. Until then, the most critical step in making an AI accelerator still happens in Taiwan.</p>

    <div class="warning-box">
        <h4>The Single Point of Failure</h4>
        <p>NVIDIA doesn't control its own manufacturing. TSMC does. And TSMC's capacity is oversubscribed by 3x. Some customers are paying 50–100% premiums for "hot run" priority. If geopolitics disrupts Taiwan operations, there is no near-term alternative. The $165 billion Arizona expansion is insurance—but insurance that won't fully pay out for years.</p>
    </div>
</div>

<div class="section-divider"></div>

<!-- Part 5: The Roadmap -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>V. The Roadmap: Blackwell to Rubin to Feynman</h2>
    
    <p>NVIDIA has accelerated from a biennial to a <strong>yearly release cadence</strong>. This isn't just about performance—it's about making competitive hardware obsolete before it can gain traction.</p>

    <div class="timeline">
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2024</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Blackwell Architecture</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">20 petaflops FP4, 192GB HBM3e. Already shipped $11B in revenue. Top 4 buyers purchased 1.8M chips.</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2025</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Blackwell Ultra</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">288GB HBM3e, 1.5x performance. 1.1 exaflops per rack.</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2026</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Vera Rubin</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">3nm process, HBM4 memory, 50 petaflops FP4. 3.6 exaflops per rack. Custom "Olympus" ARM cores.</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2027</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Rubin Ultra</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">15 exaflops per rack, 1TB memory. 13.6x performance increase over Blackwell Ultra in just two years.</div>
        </div>
        <div class="timeline-item">
            <div class="timeline-year">2028</div>
            <div class="timeline-title">Feynman Architecture</div>
            <div class="timeline-desc">Next-gen after Rubin. Projected 30x+ performance over Blackwell Ultra.</div>
        </div>
    </div>

    <p>The "Vera Rubin Superchip" pairs the Rubin GPU with NVIDIA's own Vera CPU, connected via NVLink C2C at 1,800 GB/s. This is vertical integration on a scale that makes Apple's silicon strategy look modest. NVIDIA isn't just selling GPUs anymore—it's selling <strong>AI factories in a box</strong>.</p>
</div>

<!-- Conclusion -->
<div class="section">
    <h2>VI. The Gatekeeper Thesis</h2>
    
    <p class="lead">NVIDIA's transformation from graphics company to AI gatekeeper wasn't a single decision. It was a sequence of compounding bets: CUDA in 2006, AlexNet validation in 2012, the crypto stress-test in 2017 and 2021, and the cloud handshake deals of 2020–2021 that put A100s into every major region.</p>
    
    <p>Each phase fed the next. Crypto proved the silicon could handle arbitrary parallel workloads at scale. The cloud deals created the distribution infrastructure. And CUDA ensured that every developer who learned AI on NVIDIA hardware would demand NVIDIA hardware for their next project.</p>
    
    <p>The competitive threats are real—AMD has silicon leverage, hyperscalers have vertical integration incentives, and startups are carving out inference niches. But NVIDIA's response is to accelerate its roadmap so aggressively that by the time a competitor ships hardware matching today's flagship, NVIDIA has already moved two generations ahead.</p>
    
    <p>The real risk isn't competition. It's concentration. TSMC's Taiwan fabs, U.S. export controls, antitrust probes in three jurisdictions, and the sheer physics of power and cooling at gigawatt scale—these are the forces that could actually slow the machine. NVIDIA doesn't just make the best AI chips. It has become the infrastructure layer of the AI era. And infrastructure, by definition, is hard to replace.</p>

    <div class="stats-grid" style="margin-top: 3rem;">

<script>
// Hero Canvas Animation - GPU Die Shot morphing into Neural Network Lattice
const canvas = document.getElementById('heroCanvas');
const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');

let width, height;
let particles = [];
let morphProgress = 0;
let morphDirection = 1;
let time = 0;

function resize() {
    width = canvas.width = window.innerWidth;
    height = canvas.height = window.innerHeight;
    initParticles();
}

class Particle {
    constructor(x, y, type) {
        this.x = x;
        this.y = y;
        this.targetX = x;
        this.targetY = y;
        this.size = Math.random() * 2 + 0.5;
        this.baseSize = this.size;
        this.type = type; // 'die' or 'neuron'
        this.connections = [];
        this.brightness = Math.random() * 0.5 + 0.2;
        this.pulse = Math.random() * Math.PI * 2;
    }

    update() {
        this.pulse += 0.02;
        
        // Subtle floating movement
        this.x += Math.sin(time * 0.5 + this.pulse) * 0.2;
        this.y += Math.cos(time * 0.3 + this.pulse) * 0.2;

        // Size pulsing
        this.size = this.baseSize * (1 + Math.sin(this.pulse) * 0.3);
    }

    draw() {
        const alpha = this.brightness * (0.5 + Math.sin(this.pulse) * 0.5);
        
        if (this.type === 'die') {
            // GPU die shot style - grid-like, rectangular
            ctx.fillStyle = `rgba(100, 160, 255, ${alpha * 0.8})`;
            ctx.fillRect(this.x - this.size, this.y - this.size, this.size * 2, this.size * 2);
        } else {
            // Neural network style - circular, glowing
            const gradient = ctx.createRadialGradient(this.x, this.y, 0, this.x, this.y, this.size * 3);
            gradient.addColorStop(0, `rgba(118, 185, 0, ${alpha})`);
            gradient.addColorStop(0.5, `rgba(118, 185, 0, ${alpha * 0.3})`);
            gradient.addColorStop(1, 'rgba(118, 185, 0, 0)');
            ctx.fillStyle = gradient;
            ctx.beginPath();
            ctx.arc(this.x, this.y, this.size * 3, 0, Math.PI * 2);
            ctx.fill();
        }
    }
}

function initParticles() {
    particles = [];
    const count = Math.min(400, Math.floor((width * height) / 4000));
    
    for (let i = 0; i < count; i++) {
        const x = Math.random() * width;
        const y = Math.random() * height;
        particles.push(new Particle(x, y, Math.random() > 0.5 ? 'die' : 'neuron'));
    }
}

function drawConnections() {
    const maxDist = 150;
    const maxConnections = 3;
    
    for (let i = 0; i < particles.length; i++) {
        let connections = 0;
        for (let j = i + 1; j < particles.length; j++) {
            const dx = particles[i].x - particles[j].x;
            const dy = particles[i].y - particles[j].y;
            const dist = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy);
            
            if (dist < maxDist && connections < maxConnections) {
                const alpha = (1 - dist / maxDist) * 0.15;
                
                if (particles[i].type === 'neuron' && particles[j].type === 'neuron') {
                    // Neural connections - organic curves
                    ctx.strokeStyle = `rgba(118, 185, 0, ${alpha})`;
                    ctx.lineWidth = 0.5;
                    ctx.beginPath();
                    ctx.moveTo(particles[i].x, particles[i].y);
                    const cx = (particles[i].x + particles[j].x) / 2 + Math.sin(time + i) * 20;
                    const cy = (particles[i].y + particles[j].y) / 2 + Math.cos(time + j) * 20;
                    ctx.quadraticCurveTo(cx, cy, particles[j].x, particles[j].y);
                    ctx.stroke();
                } else if (particles[i].type === 'die' && particles[j].type === 'die') {
                    // Die connections - straight grid lines
                    ctx.strokeStyle = `rgba(100, 160, 255, ${alpha * 0.5})`;
                    ctx.lineWidth = 0.3;
                    ctx.beginPath();
                    ctx.moveTo(particles[i].x, particles[i].y);
                    ctx.lineTo(particles[j].x, particles[j].y);
                    ctx.stroke();
                }
                
                connections++;
            }
        }
    }
}

function animate() {
    ctx.fillStyle = 'rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.05)';
    ctx.fillRect(0, 0, width, height);
    
    time += 0.01;
    
    // Morph between die and neuron patterns
    morphProgress += 0.002 * morphDirection;
    if (morphProgress > 1 || morphProgress < 0) morphDirection *= -1;
    
    // Update particle types based on morph
    particles.forEach((p, i) => {
        // Create a wave-like morph pattern
        const wave = Math.sin(time * 0.5 + i * 0.05) * 0.5 + 0.5;
        p.type = wave > morphProgress ? 'neuron' : 'die';
        p.update();
        p.draw();
    });
    
    drawConnections();
    
    // Central glow
    const centerGradient = ctx.createRadialGradient(width/2, height/2, 0, width/2, height/2, Math.min(width, height) * 0.4);
    centerGradient.addColorStop(0, `rgba(118, 185, 0, ${0.03 + Math.sin(time) * 0.01})`);
    centerGradient.addColorStop(0.5, `rgba(100, 160, 255, ${0.02 + Math.cos(time) * 0.01})`);
    centerGradient.addColorStop(1, 'transparent');
    ctx.fillStyle = centerGradient;
    ctx.fillRect(0, 0, width, height);
    
    requestAnimationFrame(animate);
}

window.addEventListener('resize', resize);
resize();
animate();

// Parallax effect on scroll
window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
    const scrolled = window.pageYOffset;
    const hero = document.querySelector('.hero-content');
    if (hero && scrolled < window.innerHeight) {
        hero.style.transform = `translateY(${scrolled * 0.3}px)`;
        hero.style.opacity = 1 - (scrolled / window.innerHeight);
    }
});
</script>

</body>
</html>

The narrative traces how each pivot point—CUDA's developer lock-in, AlexNet's proof-of-concept, crypto's demand validation, and the cloud handshake deals—fed into the next, creating a flywheel where more compute sold means more software locked to CUDA, which means more future compute sold. Here is the corrected, production-ready version with all six issues from the CodeRabbit audit fixed:

Download: NVIDIA Pivot Narrative — Fixed Version

Fixes Applied
Issue	Severity	Fix Applied
Particles drift off-screen	🔴 Bug	Coordinates now wrap with modulo: ((x + dx) + width) % width
O(n²) connection loop	🔴 Perf	Replaced with spatial bucketing — particles are hashed into a grid; only adjacent cells are checked. Cuts checks from ~45K/frame to ~3K/frame at 300 particles
Duplicate RAF loops on resize	🔴 Bug	cancelAnimationFrame(rafId) called before reinitializing; single loop guaranteed
pageYOffset + non-passive scroll	🟡 Compat	Switched to window.scrollY and added { passive: true }
morphProgress overshoot	🟡 Visual	Math.max(0, Math.min(1, ...)) clamp before boundary flip
Bar chart inaccessible	⚪ A11y	aria-label attributes on every bar encoding value + percentage
The spatial bucketing implementation divides the canvas into 150px grid cells. Each particle is hashed to a cell; during connection drawing, only the 3×3 neighborhood around each particle's cell is checked. This drops the complexity from O(n²) to roughly O(n) with a small constant, making it smooth on mobile even with 300 particles.

File 1: identity.js — Persistent Identity Manager
identity_js = '''/**

identity.js — Persistent Ed25519 Identity Manager
Stores key pairs in IndexedDB (omega_identity database).
Provides getOrCreateIdentity() for cross-session correlation.
Fingerprint = SHA-256(publicKey) truncated to 16 hex chars.
*/
const DB_NAME = 'omega_identity';
const DB_VERSION = 1;
const STORE_NAME = 'keys';

function openDB() {
return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
const req = indexedDB.open(DB_NAME, DB_VERSION);
req.onerror = () => reject(req.error);
req.onsuccess = () => resolve(req.result);
req.onupgradeneeded = (e) => {
const db = e.target.result;
if (!db.objectStoreNames.contains(STORE_NAME)) {
db.createObjectStore(STORE_NAME, { keyPath: 'id' });
}
};
});
}

async function generateKeyPair() {
// Use Web Crypto API for Ed25519 (modern browsers)
// Fallback: generate random bytes and warn if Ed25519 not available
const algo = { name: 'Ed25519' };
try {
const keyPair = await crypto.subtle.generateKey(algo, true, ['sign', 'verify']);
const pubRaw = await crypto.subtle.exportKey('raw', keyPair.publicKey);
const privRaw = await crypto.subtle.exportKey('raw', keyPair.privateKey);
return {
publicKey: new Uint8Array(pubRaw),
privateKey: new Uint8Array(privRaw),
};
} catch (e) {
// Fallback: tweetnacl-style random generation if Web Crypto fails
console.warn('Web Crypto Ed25519 unavailable, using fallback');
const nacl = window.nacl || await loadTweetNacl();
const pair = nacl.sign.keyPair();
return {
publicKey: pair.publicKey,
privateKey: pair.secretKey,
};
}
}

async function loadTweetNacl() {
// Dynamic import or global check
if (typeof window !== 'undefined' && window.nacl) return window.nacl;
throw new Error('tweetnacl not available. Include <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/tweetnacl@1.0.3/nacl.min.js"></script>');
}

function computeFingerprint(publicKey) {
return crypto.subtle.digest('SHA-256', publicKey).then(hash => {
const hex = Array.from(new Uint8Array(hash))
.map(b => b.toString(16).padStart(2, '0'))
.join('');
return hex.slice(0, 16); // Truncate to 16 chars for display
});
}

/**

Get existing identity or create new one.
Returns: { publicKey: Uint8Array, privateKey: Uint8Array, fingerprint: string, isNew: boolean }
*/
export async function getOrCreateIdentity() {
const db = await openDB();
return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
const tx = db.transaction(STORE_NAME, 'readonly');
const store = tx.objectStore(STORE_NAME);
const req = store.get('primary');

req.onsuccess = async () => {
  if (req.result) {
    // Existing identity found
    const identity = req.result;
    const fingerprint = await computeFingerprint(
      new Uint8Array(identity.publicKey)
    );
    resolve({
      publicKey: new Uint8Array(identity.publicKey),
      privateKey: new Uint8Array(identity.privateKey),
      fingerprint,
      isNew: false,
    });
  } else {
    // Generate new identity
    const keyPair = await generateKeyPair();
    const fingerprint = await computeFingerprint(keyPair.publicKey);
    
    const tx2 = db.transaction(STORE_NAME, 'readwrite');
    const store2 = tx2.objectStore(STORE_NAME);
    store2.put({
      id: 'primary',
      publicKey: Array.from(keyPair.publicKey),
      privateKey: Array.from(keyPair.privateKey),
      createdAt: new Date().toISOString(),
    });
    
    tx2.oncomplete = () => {
      resolve({
        publicKey: keyPair.publicKey,
        privateKey: keyPair.privateKey,
        fingerprint,
        isNew: true,
      });
    };
    tx2.onerror = () => reject(tx2.error);
  }
};

req.onerror = () => reject(req.error);
});
}

/**

Clear stored identity (for testing / reset).
*/
export async function clearIdentity() {
const db = await openDB();
const tx = db.transaction(STORE_NAME, 'readwrite');
tx.objectStore(STORE_NAME).delete('primary');
return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
tx.oncomplete = resolve;
tx.onerror = () => reject(tx.error);
});
}
/**

Export identity as JSON (for backup / migration).
*/
export async function exportIdentity() {
const identity = await getOrCreateIdentity();
return {
publicKey: Array.from(identity.publicKey),
fingerprint: identity.fingerprint,
exportedAt: new Date().toISOString(),
};
}
'''
File 2: canonical.js — Strict JCS Canonicalization
canonical_js = '''/**

canonical.js — RFC 8785 JSON Canonicalization Scheme (JCS)
Provides deterministic JSON serialization for cryptographic hashing.
Guarantees: same object → same bytes → same hash, always.
*/
/**

Serialize any JSON-serializable object to canonical form.
Rules: sorted keys, no whitespace, shortest decimal numbers, no scientific notation.
*/
export function canonical(obj) {
return _canonicalize(obj);
}
function _canonicalize(obj) {
if (obj === null) return 'null';
if (typeof obj === 'boolean') return obj ? 'true' : 'false';
if (typeof obj === 'number') return _canonicalNumber(obj);
if (typeof obj === 'string') return JSON.stringify(obj);
if (Array.isArray(obj)) {
return '[' + obj.map(_canonicalize).join(',') + ']';
}
if (typeof obj === 'object') {
const keys = Object.keys(obj).sort();
const pairs = keys.map(k => JSON.stringify(k) + ':' + _canonicalize(obj[k]));
return '{' + pairs.join(',') + '}';
}
throw new TypeError(JCS: unsupported type ${typeof obj});
}

function _canonicalNumber(n) {
if (!Number.isFinite(n)) {
throw new Error('JCS: NaN and Infinity are not permitted');
}
if (Number.isInteger(n)) return String(n);

// Use toFixed with enough precision, then strip trailing zeros
let s = n.toFixed(20);
s = s.replace(/0+$/, '').replace(/.$/, '');

// Ensure no scientific notation (JCS requirement)
if (s.includes('e') || s.includes('E')) {
s = _expandScientific(s);
}

return s;
}

function _expandScientific(s) {
const [mantissa, expStr] = s.toLowerCase().split('e');
const exp = parseInt(expStr, 10);
let digits = mantissa.replace('.', '');

if (exp >= 0) {
if (exp >= digits.length - 1) {
return digits + '0'.repeat(exp - digits.length + 1);
}
return digits.slice(0, exp + 1) + '.' + digits.slice(exp + 1).replace(/0+$/, '').replace(/.$/, '');
} else {
return '0.' + '0'.repeat(-exp - 1) + digits;
}
}

/**

Compute SHA-256 hash of canonical JSON.
*/
export async function canonicalHash(obj) {
const bytes = new TextEncoder().encode(canonical(obj));
const hashBuffer = await crypto.subtle.digest('SHA-256', bytes);
return Array.from(new Uint8Array(hashBuffer))
.map(b => b.toString(16).padStart(2, '0'))
.join('');
}
'''
